## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: chemical kinetics
**Analysis**: This task models reaction rate dA/dt as a function of concentration A and time t, belonging to chemical reaction kinetics. The rate law likely involves power-law dependence on A, possibly with explicit time dependence from hidden variables or external forcing.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Zero-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 (constant rate, independent of concentration)
- First-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A (radioactive decay, simple decomposition)
- Second-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 (bimolecular reaction of same species)
- nth-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 (general power-law rate law)
- Reversible first-order: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 (approach to equilibrium with constant back-reaction)
- Michaelis-Menten type: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A) (enzyme kinetics, surface catalysis)
- Autocatalytic with decay: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * A**2 (autocatalytic or dimerization pathway)
- Langmuir-Hinshelwood: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A)**2 (competitive surface adsorption kinetics)
- Mixed order: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A**c2) (generalized saturation kinetics)
- Time-dependent rate: dA_dt = c0 * A * exp(c1 * t) (time-varying rate constant, e.g., temperature ramp)
- Parallel pathways: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * A**c2 (competing first and nth order reactions)
- Inhibition kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A + c2 * A**2) (substrate inhibition)
- Power-law with time modulation: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 * t**c2 (fractal or dispersive kinetics)
- Sigmoidal rate: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 / (c2 + A**c1) (cooperative or Hill-type kinetics)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Concentration power-law dependence → dA/dt ~ A^n indicates reaction molecularity or effective order n
- Rational function of concentration → saturation kinetics from enzyme or surface site limitation (Michaelis-Menten form)
- Negative linear term plus positive nonlinear term → reversible or competing forward/backward reactions
- Explicit time dependence in rate → suggests hidden intermediate species or externally varying conditions (temperature, light)
- Quadratic concentration terms → bimolecular steps or autocatalytic feedback in mechanism
- Denominator with polynomial in A → adsorption/desorption equilibria or quasi-steady-state intermediates
- Product of A and (1-A/c) terms → logistic-like growth with carrying capacity, common in autocatalysis with finite substrate
- Fractional power of A (A^0.5) → dissociative mechanisms or radical chain reactions
- Sum of distinct power-law terms → parallel reaction pathways with different orders
- Rate proportional to A*ln(A) → nucleation-growth kinetics (Avrami-type differential form)

**Candidate 24**: `A*c0 + A*c1/(A + c2)**2 + A*c3*exp(c4*t) + c5 + c6*cos(c7*log(A*c8 + 1))`

The sin term in GT vs cos here. Note sin(x) = cos(x - π/2). But the argument here is `c7*log(A*c8+1)` with no phase shift inside cos. We need `sin(log(A+1)) = cos(something*log(A+1))` for all A, which isn't possible since sin ≠ cos with just a scaling of the argument.
